     205             : /************************************************************************/
     206             : /**
     207             :  * \brief Destroy feature
     208             :  *
     209             :  * The feature is deleted, but within the context of the GDAL/OGR heap.
     210             :  * This is necessary when higher level applications use GDAL/OGR from a
     211             :  * DLL and they want to delete a feature created within the DLL.  If the
     212             :  * delete is done in the calling application the memory will be freed onto
     213             :  * the application heap which is inappropriate.
     214             :  *
     215             :  * This function is the same as the C++ method OGRFeature::DestroyFeature().
     216             :  *
     217             :  * @param hFeat handle to the feature to destroy.
     218             :  */

     343             :  *
     344             :  * This method updates the features geometry, and operate exactly as
     345             :  * SetGeometry(), except that this method assumes ownership of the
     346             :  * passed geometry (even in case of failure of that function).
     347             :  *
     348             :  * This method is the same as the C function OGR_F_SetGeometryDirectly().
     349             :  *
     350             :  * @note This method has only an effect on the in-memory feature object. If
     351             :  * this object comes from a layer and the modifications must be serialized back
     352             :  * to the datasource, OGR_L_SetFeature() must be used afterwards. Or if this is
     353             :  * a new feature, OGR_L_CreateFeature() must be used afterwards.
     354             :  *
     355             :  * @param poGeomIn new geometry to apply to feature. Passing NULL value here
     356             :  * is correct and it will result in deallocation of currently assigned geometry
     357             :  * without assigning new one.
     358             :  *
     359             :  * @return OGRERR_NONE if successful, or OGR_UNSUPPORTED_GEOMETRY_TYPE if

    6695             : 
    6696             : /**
    6697             :  * \fn const char* OGRFeature::GetNativeData() const;
    6698             :  *
    6699             :  * \brief Returns the native data for the feature.
    6700             :  *
    6701             :  * The native data is the representation in a "natural" form that comes from
    6702             :  * the driver that created this feature, or that is aimed at an output driver.
    6703             :  * The native data may be in different format, which is indicated by
    6704             :  * GetNativeMediaType().
    6705             :  *
    6706             :  * Note that most drivers do not support storing the native data in the feature
    6707             :  * object, and if they do, generally the NATIVE_DATA open option must be passed
    6708             :  * at dataset opening.
    6709             :  *
    6710             :  * The "native data" does not imply it is something more performant or powerful
    6711             :  * than what can be obtained with the rest of the API, but it may be useful in
    6712             :  * round-tripping scenarios where some characteristics of the underlying format
    6713             :  * are not captured otherwise by the OGR abstraction.
    6714             :  *
    6715             :  * This function is the same as the C function
    6716             :  * OGR_F_GetNativeData().
    6717             :  *
    6718             :  * @return a string with the native data, or NULL if there is none.
    6719             :  * @since GDAL 2.1
    6720             :  *
    6721             :  * @see https://trac.osgeo.org/gdal/wiki/rfc60_improved_roundtripping_in_ogr
    6722             :  */
    6723             :
